рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рд╖реН рдЯреАрдХрд╛рдГ ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton

60 (669)
Agni
Bharga Prag─Бtha
20 verses: br╠еhat─л alternating with satobr╠еhat─л, arranged in prag─Бthas
The focus throughout most of this hymn is Agni in his sacrificial role, a theme strongly established in the first five verses, and in his close relationship to the household and clan. As a consequence of this latter relationship he also appears as the protector of those entities against external threats: see verses 6тАУ10, 12тАУ14, and especially the two final verses 19тАУ20. The usual prayers for wealth and aid are not absent, however.

English translation:

тАЬAgni, come here with the fires, we choose you as our invoking priest; let the presented offering anointyou, the chief sacrificer, to sit down on the sacred grass.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Agni, drive here with your fires: we would choose you as our Hotar. Let the oblation-bearing (ladle), held forth, anoint you, the best
sacrificer, for you to sit upon the ritual grass,

Griffith

AGNI, come hither with thy fires; we choose thee as Invoking Priest.
Let the extended ladle full of oil balm thee, best Priest, to sit on sacred grass.

Geldner

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAс╣Еgirasa, son of strength, the ladles go to find you in the sacrifice; we praise the ancient Agni in ourofferings, the grandson of food, butter-haired.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Butter-haired: Agni is called ghс╣Ыtapс╣Ыс╣гс╣нh─Б, ‘butter-backed’ (RV.5.4.3); prad─лpta kala┼Ыa sth─Бn─лya jv─Бl─Бс╕е; prad─лpta kala┼Ыa = prad─лpta ke┼Ыa; cf. RV 5.37.1

Jamison Brereton

For the ladles are moving toward you at the ceremony, o son of strength, o Aс╣Еgiras.
We supplicate the child of nourishment, ghee-haired Agni, foremost at the sacrifices.

Griffith

For unto thee, O Angiras, O Son of Strength, move ladles in the sacrifice.
To Agni, Child of Force, whose locks drop oil, we seek, foremost in sacrificial rites.

Geldner

Denn dir, du Sohn der Kraft, Angiras, nahen die L├╢ffel w├дhrend des Gottesdienstes. An das Kind der Kraft mit Schmalz im Haare wenden wir uns, an Agni als den ersten bei den Opfern.

Grassmann

Denn zu dir gehn, o Sohn der St├дrke, Angiras, die L├╢ffel bei dem Opfer hin; Den Spross der Kraft, den Agni mit dem Fett im Haar, ihn flehn zuerst bei Opfern wir.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni, you, wise, are the creator (of consequences); O purifier, you are the involving priest, worthy ofworship; bright one, you are to be praised in our sacrifices by the priests with hymns, yourself the chief ministrantworthy to be rejoiced in.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O Agni, pure one, you are the sage poet and ritual expert, the Hotar who receives (the command) тАЬsacrifice!тАЭтАФ
delightful, the best sacrificer, to be invoked at the ceremonies by our inspired poets with their thoughts, o blazing one.

Griffith

Agni, thou art Disposer, Sage, Herald, bright God! and worshipful,
Best offercr, cheerful, to be praised in holy rites, pure Lord! by singers with their hymns.

Geldner

Agni, du bist der Seher, der Meister, der wunderbare Hotri, du Lauterer, wohlredend, bestopfernd, im Gottesdienst von den Redekundigen mit Gebeten anzurufen, du Heller.

Grassmann

Als weiser Ordner strahlest du, als rascher Priester, Flammender, Aufs beste opfernd, hold bei Festen, preisenswerth durch fromme Lieder, Agni du.

Elizarenkova

Just you, of great extent, are the entruthed sage poet, o guardian Agni. Just you do the inspired poets and the ritual experts seek to attract here, o you who shine while being kindled.

English translation:

тАЬMost resplendent (Agni), shine forth and illuminate (us); give happiness to your people, to yourworshipper, for you are great; may my priests abide in the bliss of the gods, subduing their enemies, possessingbright fires.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

My priests: s┼лrayaс╕е = stotaro medh─Бvinaс╕е asm─Бkam putr─Бdayo v─Б

Jamison Brereton

Blaze bright, brightest blazing one; shine joy for the clan. Give to the praiser. You are great!
Let my patrons, overpowering their rivals and endowed with good fires, be under the shelter of the gods.

Griffith

Shine, Most Resplendent! blaze, send bliss unto the folk, and to thy worshipper
Great art thou.
So may my princes, with good fires, subduing foes, rest in the keeping of the Gods.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAs, Agni, you consume old timber on the earth, so, cherisher of friends, do you burn our injurer,whosoever evil-minded wishes (our ill).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Just as you incinerate the brushwood grown thick on the ground, o Agni,
in the same way burn whoever stalks (us), lying to us and
ill-intentioned, o you who deploy the might of alliance.

Griffith

O Agni, as thou burnest down to earth even high-grown underwood,
So, bright as Mitra is, burn him who injures us, him who plots ill against thy friend.

Geldner

Wie du, Agni, auch das gro├Яgewordene Gestr├╝pp auf dem Erdboden verbrennst, so versenge du, wie Mitra Geehrter, jeden, der uns ├Ьbel will, der in b├╢ser Absicht scheel sieht.

Grassmann

Wie, Agni, du auch gross Gestr├╝pp verzehrest auf der Erde Grund, So brenn, o freundereicher, den, der uns verfolgt, der b├╢sgesinnt uns schaden will.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬSubject us not to a strong mortal enemy, nor to the malevolent; O most youthful, guard us with yourunharming delivering auspicious protections.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Do not make us subject to a mortal who is a cheat possessed of demonic power, nor to one who utters evil.
O youngest one, protect us with your protectors that are unfailing, overwhelming, but kindly.

Griffith

Give us not as a prey to mortal enemy, nor to the wicked friend of fiends.
With conquering guards, auspicious, unassailable, protect us, O Most Youthful God.

Geldner

Gib uns nicht dem betr├╝gerischen, t├╝ckischen Sterblichen, nicht dem ├Ьbelredenden in die Hand! Sch├╝tze uns, du J├╝ngster, mit deinen nie fehlenden, durchhelfenden, freundlichen Sch├╝tzern!

Grassmann

Nicht gib uns preis dem Menschen, der uns feindlich ist, noch unheilvollem Zauberer, Mit raschen H├╝tern, die uns heilsam, freundlich sind, besch├╝tze du, o j├╝ngster, uns.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬAgni, protect us by one (rich), or protect us by a second; lord of strength, protect us by three sons;protect us, giver of dwellings, by four.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Four: с╣Ыk, yajuс╣г, s─Бman and nigada

Jamison Brereton

Protect us with one, Agni, and protect us with a second.
Protect us with three hymns, o lord of nourishments; protect us with four, o good one. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

I am a little uncertain why/how Agni protects us with hymn(s) (g├нr-), which are what we usually offer to him. Geldner and Renou soften the expression by tr.

тАШword(s)тАЩ, but that is not what g├нr- means. Perhaps AgniтАЩs тАЬhymnsтАЭ are the crackling noises of the fire, or else the instrumentals express cause: тАЬprotect us by reason of (our) hymns.тАЭ I prefer the former of these solutions. (See 18a below.) The various instrumentals cannot directly take up the p─Бy├║bhiс╕е of 8d, because p─Бy├║- is masc. and all four number instrumentals (├йkay─Б, etc.) are unambiguously feminine, as is g├нrwhen it finally shows up in c.

Griffith

Protect us, Agni, through the first, protect us through the second hymn,

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬProtect us from every impious r─Бkс╣гasa, shield us in battles; we approach you, our nearest neighbour,our kinsman, for sacrifice and for increase.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Impious: not giving (sacrificial) gifts

Jamison Brereton

Protect us from every hostile demon. Ever further us when prizes (are at stake),
for we approach just you, the one nearest to the divine assemblage and our friend, for strengthening.

Griffith

Preserve us from each fiend who brings the Gods no gift, preserve thou us in deeds of strength:

English translation:

тАЬPurifying Agni, bestow upon us food-augmenting excellent wealth; and (bring) us, O meter-out of good,by auspicious guidance, (a treasure) desired by many and bringing its own fame.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(Bring) here to us praiseworthy wealth that strengthens vital force, o pure Agni,
and give it to us, o apportionerтАФ(wealth) much craved and very gloriousтАФwith your good guidanceтАФ с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

A verb like тАШbringтАЩ needs to be supplied with the first hemistich based on the numerous passages containing ─Б╠Бbhara governing no ray├нm (e.g., I.79.8 ─Б╠Бno agne ray├нm bhara); cf. also 18cd below. On upam─Бte see VIII.40.9.

The published translation тАЬvery gloriousтАЭ is a careless error for тАЬself-glorious,тАЭ misreading sv├бya┼Ыastaram as *s├║ya┼Ыastaram. I am evidently not alone in this, as the SV reads this instead. If this were the correct reading the accent should probably have been

*suy├б┼Ыastaram, given forms like su┼Ыr├бvas(-tama)-.

Griffith

O Holy Agni, give us wealth renowned with men and strengthening life.
Bestow on us, O Helper, that which many crave, more glorious still by righteousness;

Geldner

Bring uns, Agni, l├╢blichen Reichtum, der die Lebenskraft st├дrkt, du Lauterer, und schenk uns, du Zuteiler, vielbegehrten, selbstherrlichen, unter deiner guten Leitung!

Grassmann

O schenke, Agni, Reichthum uns, der Macht vermehrt, o flammender, Der preisenswerth und viel begehrt, noch herrlicher durch gute Leitung wird, o Freund,

Elizarenkova

рдпреЗрди рдзрдиреЗрди рдкреГрддрдирд╛рд╕реБ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗрд╖реБ рд╢рд░реНрдзрддрдГ рд╡реЗрдЧрдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рддрдГ рдЕрд░реНрдпрдГ рдЕрд░реАрдЮреНрдЫрддреНрд░реВрдиреН рдЖрджрд┐рд╢рдГ рдЖрджреЗрд╖реНрдЯреДрдЮреНрдЫрд╕реНрддреНрд░рдкреНрд░рдХреНрд╖реЗрдкреНрддреДрдиреН рддрд░рдиреНрддрдГ рд╡рдВрд╕рд╛рдо рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд╛рдо рддрджреНрдзрдирдВ рджреЗрд╣рд┐ ред рд╣реЗ рд╢рдЪреАрд╡рд╕реЛ рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрдЮрдпрд╛ рд╡рд╛рд╕рдпрд┐рддрдГ рдХрд░реНрдордзрди рд╡рд╛ рд╕рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдГ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рд╡рд░реНрдз рд╡рд░реНрдзрдп рдкреНрд░реАрдгрдпред рдкреНрд░рдпрд╕рд╛ рдЕрдиреНрдиреЗрди рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╡рд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдзред рдЕрд╕реНрдорджреАрдпреЗрди рдкреНрд░рдпрд╕рд╛ рд╣рд╡рд┐рд╖рд╛ рд╡рд╕реБрд╡рд┐рджрдГ рд╡рд╕реВрдирд╛рдВ рд▓рдореНрднрдХрд╛рдирд┐ рдзрд┐рдпрдГ рдХрд░реНрдорд╛рдгреНрдпрд╕реНрдорджреАрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рдЬрд┐рдиреНрд╡ рдкреНрд░реАрдгрдп рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBy which we may escape and destroy in battles our impetuous weapon- aiming enemies; O you who bywisdom establish our rites, bless us with food, prosper our wealth-obtaining offerings.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(Wealth) with which we will vanquish in battles those who vaunt themselves, as we overcome the aims of the stranger.
Strengthen us because of our pleasing offering, o you who have the goods of skill. Quicken our insights so they find goods. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner and Renou take vardha as intransitive/reflexive тАЬwachse du,тАЭ тАЬrenforce toi,тАЭ but active forms of v├бrdha- are about as reliably transitive as Vedic verbs get.

Griffith

Wherewith we may o’ercome our rivals in the war, o’erpowering the foe’s designs.
So wax thou by our food, O Excellent in strength. Quicken our thoughts that find out wealth.

Geldner

Durch den wir in den K├дmpfen die sich ├Ьberhebenden ├╝berwinden, die Bedrohungen des Nebenbuhlers durchkreuzend. Wachse du durch unsere Labung, Kraftreicher, wecke fromme Gedanken, die das Gute finden.

Grassmann

Durch den die stolzen in den K├дmpfen wir zerstreun, durchkreuzend unsrer Feinde Plan; So st├дrke du uns, kr├дftiger, durch deine Huld, lass Gut erlangen das Gebet.

English translation:

тАЬAgni tosses his horns, sharpening them as a bull; his sharp jaws are not to be resisted; he is mightytoothed, this son of strength.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Not to be resisted: na = iva (hanava iva);

Na = prat─лdhс╣Ыс╣гe

Jamison Brereton

Like a bull sharpening his horns, shaking them again and again, is Agni.
His sharp jaws are not to be withstood: well fanged is the young (son) of strength.

Agni is even as a bull who whets and brandishes his horns.
Well-sharpened are his jaws which may not be withstood: the Child of Strength hath powerful teeth.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou sleep within your mothers in the woods, mortals kindle you; unwearied you bear the offerings of thesacrificer, then you shine among the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Your mothers: the two araс╣Зis or pieces of wood from which thesacrificial fire is produced by attrition; RV 3.29.2

Jamison Brereton

You lie in the pieces of wood and in your two mothers [=kindling sticks]; the mortals kindle you.
Tireless, you convey the oblations of him who makes oblation. Right after that you shine [/rule] among the gods.

Griffith

Thou liest in the wood: from both thy Mothers mortals kindle thee.
Unweariedly thou bearest up the offerer’s gifts, then shinest bright among the Gods.

Geldner

Du liegst in den H├╢lzern, in deinen beiden M├╝ttern; die Sterblichen entz├╝nden dich. Unerm├╝dlich f├дhrst du die Opferspenden des Opferbereiters. Dann gebietest du ├╝ber die G├╢tter.

Grassmann

In H├╢lzern, deiner Mutter Schooss, liegst du, dich z├╝nden Menschen an; Des Opfers Tr├дnke f├дhrst du unerm├╝dlich hin; dann strahlest bei den G├╢ttern du.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThe seven priests praise you, Agni, giver of good things and unfailing; you cleave the cloud with yourfierce splendour; go forth, having overcome our enemies.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Jan─Бm = asm─Бn, proceed to the gods with theoblation, having left us behind

Jamison Brereton

The seven Hotars reverently invoke just you, o Agni, the unabashed one displaying great abandon.
You split apart the rock with your heat and your flame. Agni, stand out beyond the peoples. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

The sense of suty├бjam is disputed. I ascribe to it the same metaphorical meaning as тАШabandonтАЩ acquires in English, namely acting without constraint. This fits nicely with ├бhrayas- тАШunabashed, immoderate, unrestrainedтАЩ. A fire blazing up out of control is presumably meant; in the next p─Бda it manages to split a rock – a sudden glancing allusion to the Vala myth, in which Agni usually has no role.

Griffith

And so the seven priests, O Agni, worship thee, Free-giver, Everlasting One.
Thou cIeavest through the rock with heat and fervent glow. Agni, rise up above the men.

Sieben Opferpriester rufen dich darum an, Agni, den Fl├╝chtigen, der nicht sch├╝chtern ist. Du spaltest den Fels mit deiner Glut, deiner Flamme. Agni erhebe dich ├╝ber die Menschen!

Grassmann

Als solchen preisen, Agni, sieben Priester dich, den kecken, t├╝cht’gen Schleuderer, Den Fels zerbrichst du mit der Glut, mit deinem Licht dring’ ├╝ber alle Menschen vor.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(The sacrificer) worships you by praises, Agni, with the experienced (priests) in the rite celebrated withbeautiful S─Бman hymns;bring us of your own accord for our protection food of various kinds which may bealways in our reach.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He [=singer?] keeps company with your intention in the shelter made of good melody. O perceptive Agni, the *pieces of wood are for you.
By impulsion bring here to us the prize of many forms to be nearest to us, for our aid. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

In a hymn of rare clarity, this verse provides a sudden stumbling block.

RenouтАЩs comment, тАЬGalamatias [gibberish] en d─Бnastuti,тАЭ does not provoke optimism.

My interpr. is very far from the standard ones. The problems arise from the grammatical and semantic interpr. of suс╣г─Бm├бс╣Зi and of the hapax cikitv├бn─Б and the construal of sacate and of t├║bhyam.

The differently accented suс╣г─Б╠Бman- is a PN, and both Geldner and Renou take suс╣г─Бm├бni as such here (so also Mayr. PN) – Geldner as a nom. (тАЬeine der r├дtselhaften Nominativeformen auf iтАЭ) and Renou, more sensibly, as a loc. Because of the accent difference and because a PN does nothing for us, I prefer GrassmannтАЩs suggestion that it has real lexical value (тАШgood melodyтАЩ or тАШhaving good melodyтАЩ), though I confess I do not understand why it would have this particular accent. It modifies loc. ┼Ы├бrman: a тАЬshelter made of good melodyтАЭ would either be the protective power of the sung portion of the rite or the protection given by the тАЬsingingтАЭ fire (see vs. 9 above, with AgniтАЩs hymns).

As for cikitv├бn─Б, most interpr. take it as an instr. modifying k├йtena and derived in some way from тИЪcit. Oldenberg takes it as a deformation of the instr. of the pf.

part. cikit├║с╣г─Б, which is metrically impossible in the cadence; others set up a nonce stem cikitv├бn-. By contrast I think cikitv├бn─Б should be divided into two words: cikit v├бn─Б. The first belongs to the stem cik├нt- тАШperceptive, observantтАЩ (4x) found only otherwise in the nom. sg. (likewise cik├нt), twice of Agni (VIII.102.2, X.3.1). This would be its vocative, differing only in its lack of accent. What remains is v├бn─Б, which can be the neut. pl. of v├бna- тАШ(piece of) woodтАЩ (see 15a above), which is found here in a possessive constr. with dat. t├║bhyam. In external sandhi we should, of course, have expected *cikid v├бna, but I think the multiple exx. of cikitv─Б╠Бn, cikitvas, etc., could have produced a redactional change, once voc. cikit was no longer clearly understood. (In the published translation an asterisk should precede тАЬO perceptive AgniтАЭ as well as тАЬpieces of wood.тАЭ) Taking t├║bhyam as part of an independent clause solves another problem in the other interpr., for there is no good way to construe it with p─Бda a. Geldner must take it as an honorary gen. with ┼Ы├бrman (тАЬin deiner ObhutтАЭ), but though the dative can express possession in predicative usage, I do not think this is possible in attributive usage. Renou construes it instead with sacate, тАЬ(le po├иte) t’ob├йit,тАЭ positing what I consider an unprecedented case frame (dat. only) and meaning for s├бcate. (The parallel he adduces, V.43.15, is to be taken differently, and in fact Renou does not tr. it in parallel fashion himself.) With t├║bhyam belonging to another clause, sacate is free to be construed with the instr., as it regularly is. The instr. in question is k├йta- тАШwill, intentionтАЩ, which is regularly governed by ├бnu тИЪi тАШfollowтАЩ (IV.26.2, etc.), semantically very close to тАШkeep company with, be accompanied byтАЩ; cf. also keta-s├бp- (V.38.3) тАШserving the willтАЩ.

Geldner renders iс╣гaс╣Зy├бy─Б as тАШnach WunschтАЩ, hence presumably to тИЪiс╣г тАШdesireтАЩ, but it seems arbitrary to separate it from the verb stem iс╣гaс╣Зy├б- тАШsend, impel, driveтАЩ.

Griffith

Agni, with noble psalm that tells his wish he dwells, thinking on thee who guardest him.
Speedily bring us strength of many varied sorts to be most near to succour us.

English translation:

тАЬDivine Agni, worthy of praise, you are the guardian of men, the consumer of the r─Бkс╣гasas; you aregreat, you the never-absent guardian of the (worshipper’s) house, the protector of heaven, ever present in thedwelling.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Worthy of praise: jaritr. = the singer of praises; i.e. Agni = stutya

Jamison Brereton

O Agni, o singer and god, you are the clanlord who burns the demons, the houselord who doesnтАЩt go abroad; you are greatтАФthe protector
from heaven, but devoted to the house.

Mighty art thou, the ever-present Household-Lord, Home-friend and Guardian from the sky.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬO you brilliant wealth, let not the r─Бkс╣гasa enter us, nor the torment of the evil spirits; Agni, drive awayfurther than a gavy┼лti from us poverty, hunger and the strong demons.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Gavy┼лti: this is a measure = twokro┼Ыas; it implies an unlimited distance;

Hunger: kс╣гudham = ksapayit─Бram, the destroyer

Jamison Brereton

Let demonic power not enter into us, nor the sorcery of those who deploy sorcery, o you who have the goods of the glowing one
[=P┼лс╣гan].
Keep thirst and hunger away, far beyond the pasture-lands; o Agni,
keep away those who deploy demonic power. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

The voc. ─Бghс╣Ыс╣З─лvaso is taken lit. by Geldner and Renou (тАШGlutreicherтАЩ and тАШriche en ardeur-de-feuтАЩ respectively). But ─Б╠Бghr╠ес╣Зi- is an epithet exclusively of P┼лс╣гan, and it is highly unlikely that it would be used only here, in this awkward compound, without that reference. So it must mean тАШwho has the goods of P┼лс╣гanтАЩ – presumably the cows and other domestic stuff that are appropriate to this last prag─Бtha.

Griffith

Let no fiend come among us, O thou rich in light, no spell of those who deal in spells.
To distant pastures drive faint hunger: far away, O Agni, chase the demons’ friends.

Geldner

Nicht soll ein b├╢ser Geist in mich fahren, du Glutreicher, nicht der Zauber der Zauberer. Halte ├╝ber eine Gavyuti weit ab die D├╝rre, den Hunger, die t├╝ckischen Menschen, Agni!

Nicht dringe Unheil zu uns ein, o gl├╝hender, noch Zauberei der Zauberer; Entkr├дftung, Hunger treibe fort aus unsrer Flur, o, Agni, und der Feinde Schar.
